        </div><div class="casAbstract">Traditional metal anode materials in lithium-ion batteries are plagued by instability upon discharge-charge cycling.  We report that a unique sandwiched Zn2GeO4-graphene oxide nanocomposite has been synthesized on a large scale through a simple ion-exchange reaction, whereby Zn2GeO4 nanorods with lengths of 600 nm and widths of 40 nm are homogeneously sandwiched into the graphene oxide matrix.  Compared with bare Zn2GeO4 nanorods, a dramatic improvement in the electrochem. performance of the resulting nanocomposite has been achieved.  In the voltage window of 0.001-3 V, the electrode of the Zn2GeO4-graphene oxide nanocomposite delivers a specific capacity as high as 1150 mA h g-1 at 200 mA g-1 after 100 discharge-charge cycles.  Even at a high c.d. of 3.2 A g-1, a capacity of 522 mA h g-1 can be retained.  The unusual electrochem. performance including highly reversible capacity and excellent rate capability arise from synergetic chem. coupling effects between Zn2GeO4 and graphene oxide.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrIkg4tVvn4abVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhVIvuMHb03rw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvFOjs7nF&amp;md5=034e87ef9c04dc22a079b1c2f34a6fe1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1039/C1EE02831F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luan, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Madhavi, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lou, X.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene/metal oxide composite electrode materials for energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Zhong-Shuai; Zhou, Guangmin; Yin, Li-Chang; Ren, Wencai; Li, Feng; Cheng, Hui-Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Recent progress on graphene/metal oxide composites as advanced electrode materials in lithium ion batteries (LIBs) and electrochem. capacitors (ECs) is described, highlighting the importance of synergistic effects between graphene and metal oxides and the beneficial role of graphene in composites for LIBs and ECs.  It is demonstrated that, when the composites are used as electrode materials for LIBs and ECs, compared to their individual constituents, graphene/metal oxide composites with unique structural variables such as anchored, wrapped, encapsulated, sandwich, layered and mixed models have a significant improvement in their electrochem. properties such as high capacity, high rate capability and excellent cycling stability.  First, an introduction on the properties, synthesis strategies and use of graphene is briefly given, followed by a state-of-the-art review on the prepn. of graphene/metal oxide composites and their electrochem. properties in LIBs and ECs.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical Hollow Spheres of Fe2O3@Polyaniline for Lithium Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jeong, Jae-Min; Choi, Bong Gill; Lee, Soon Chang; Lee, Kyoung G.; Chang, Sung-Jin; Han, Young-Kyu; Lee, Young Boo; Lee, Hyun Uk; Kwon, Soonjo; Lee, Gaehang; Lee, Chang-Soo; Huh, Yun Suk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium ion batteries (LIBs) have mainly been employed as energy sources for portable electronics, and are now expanding their applications to a larger scale, particularly elec. vehicles and grid storage.  Ever increasing demand in such applications has stimulated significant interest in the development of energy storage electrode materials.  In this context, α-Fe2O3 is a non-toxic, low cost material and has a higher theor. capacity value (1007 mAh g-1) than com. graphite (372 mAh g-1).  Thus, it has been considered as one of the most promising anode candidates.  Significant capacity fading, however, is still obsd. at both high rate and long-term charge/discharge cycling due to the large sp. vol. changes during battery cycling and kinetic limitations of its intrinsic nature.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqBOFtYX2wyBbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh56rVkeq2RSQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtlansL7F&amp;md5=abd5273831ab77e87e2507f525de7bab</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1021/nl302618s"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jeong, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cho, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Spindle-like Mesoporous α-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Anode Material Prepared from MOF Template for High-Rate Lithium Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">12</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">4988</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">4991</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Spindle-like Mesoporous α-Fe2O3 Anode Material Prepared from MOF Template for High-Rate Lithium Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Xiaodong; Cao, Ruiguo; Jeong, Sookyung; Cho, Jaephil</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Spindle-like porous α-Fe2O3 was prepd. from an iron-based metal org. framework (MOF) template.  When tested as anode material for lithium batteries (LBs), this spindle-like porous α-Fe2O3 shows greatly enhanced performance of Li storage.  The particle with a length and width of ∼0.8 and ∼0.4 μm, resp., was composed of clustered Fe2O3 nanoparticles with sizes of &lt; 20 nm.  The capacity of the porous α-Fe2O3 retained 911 mAh g-1 after 50 cycles at a rate of 0.2 C.  Even when cycled at 10 C, comparable capacity of 424 mAh g-1 could be achieved.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr9crQj9SSJ1rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh56rVkeq2RSQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhtFyqtrfJ&amp;md5=0cc0f9e7084801d9664741baacf57703</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1021/ja311550t"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, S.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Performance and Ultra-Stable Lithium-Ion Batteries Based on MOF-Derived ZnO@ZnO Quantum Dots/C Core-Shell Nanorod Arrays on a Carbon Cloth Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Guanhua; Hou, Sucheng; Zhang, Hang; Zeng, Wei; Yan, Feilong; Li, Cheng Chao; Duan, Huigao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors reported a facile and scalable strategy to obtain integrated, binder-free, and light wt. ZnO nanoarray-based electrode prepd. by growing ZnO@ZnO QDs/C core-shell nanorod arrays (NRAs) on flexible carbon cloth (CC).  Applied as anode material, the as-synthesized ZnO@ZnO QDs/C core-shell NRAs manifested high specific capacity and excellent cycling performance.  The self-supported ZnO@ZnO QDs/C NRAs exhibited a remarkable rate capability (a reversible capability of 1053, 913, 762, 591, and 530 mA-h g-1 at 100, 200, 400, 800, and 1000 mA g-1, resp.) and as well as remarkable cycling performance (approx. 11% capacity loss after 100 cycles at 500 mA g-1 with, a capacity retention of 699 mA-h g-1).                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MOF-Derived Porous ZnO/ZnFe2O4/C Octahedra with Hollow Interiors for High-Rate Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zou, Feng; Hu, Xianluo; Li, Zhen; Long, Qie; Hu, Chenchen; Zeng, Rui; Jiang, Yan; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel porous ZnO/ZnFe2O4/C octahedra with hollow interiors is fabricated using metal-org. frameworks (MOF) as both the precursor and the self-sacrificing template.  The synthesis process only involves an ordinary refluxing reaction to form MOFs in soln. followed by thermal annealing in N2.  The strategy is easy, tunable, and cost-effective, and therefore it is highly promising for mass prodn.  Ultrafine ZnO and ZnFe2O4 nanocrystals of &lt; 5 nm are generated during thermal annealing of hollow MOF-5 octahedra, and these nanocrystals are simultaneously embedded in a 3D inter-connected, porous carbon framework derived from in-situ carbonization of the org. ligands.  Encouragingly, the as-synthesized novel hybrid, ZnO/ZnFe2O4/C, which has a well-defined 3D porous architecture, exhibits an outstanding electrochem. lithium-storage performance (high capacity, high power, and long cycle life) as an anode material for the lithium ion batteries, combining the advantages of ultrafine Zn-contg. oxide nanocrystals with an elastic carbon network, hollow interior structure, and high porosity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoXT1pfJwqrsLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh56rVkeq2RSQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtlKrsrrF&amp;md5=0642ffa1e348c412b77e5bd7ffef8e8f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA01966K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shao, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wan, Z.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite the great advantages of hollow structures as electrodes for lithium-ion batteries, one apparent common drawback which is often criticized is their compromised volumetric energy d. due to the introduced hollow interior.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hollow Iron Oxide Nanoparticles for Application in Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Koo, Bonil; Xiong, Hui; Slater, Michael D.; Prakapenka, Vitali B.; Balasubramanian, Mahalingam; Podsiadlo, Paul; Johnson, Christopher S.; Rajh, Tijana; Shevchenko, Elena V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Material design in terms of their morphologies other than solid nanoparticles can lead to more advanced properties.  At the example of Fe oxide, the authors explored the electrochem. properties of hollow nanoparticles with an application as a cathode and anode.  Such nanoparticles contain very high concn. of cation vacancies that can be efficiently used for reversible Li ion intercalation without structural change.  Cycling in high voltage range results in high capacity (∼132 mA-h/g at 2.5 V), 99.7% Coulombic efficiency, superior rate performance (133 mA-h/g at 3000 mA/g) and excellent stability (no fading at fast rate during &gt;500 cycles).  Cation vacancies in hollow Fe oxide nanoparticles also are responsible for the enhanced capacity in the conversion reactions.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Large-scale pattern growth of graphene films for stretchable transparent electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Keun Soo; Zhao, Yue; Jang, Houk; Lee, Sang Yoon; Kim, Jong Min; Kim, Kwang S.; Ahn, Jong-Hyun; Kim, Philip; Choi, Jae-Young; Hong, Byung Hee</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature (London, United Kingdom)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Problems assocd. with large-scale pattern growth of graphene constitute one of the main obstacles to using this material in device applications.  Recently, macroscopic-scale graphene films were prepd. by two-dimensional assembly of graphene sheets chem. derived from graphite crystals and graphene oxides.  However, the sheet resistance of these films was found to be much larger than theor. expected values.  Here we report the direct synthesis of large-scale graphene films using chem. vapor deposition on thin nickel layers, and present two different methods of patterning the films and transferring them to arbitrary substrates.  The transferred graphene films show very low sheet resistance of ∼280 Ω per square, with ∼80% optical transparency.  At low temps., the monolayers transferred to silicon dioxide substrates show electron mobility greater than 3,700 cm2 V-1 s-1 and exhibit the half-integer quantum Hall effect, implying that the quality of graphene grown by chem. vapor deposition is as high as mech. cleaved graphene.  Employing the outstanding mech. properties of graphene, we also demonstrate the macroscopic use of these highly conducting and transparent electrodes in flexible, stretchable, foldable electronics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqKGOlTbW4cmrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhQyO_zFSMv9A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1MXht1ehtL4%253D&amp;md5=0eef5b83d20b2e74add31eb1aa19337e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1021/nl801827v"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Reina, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jia, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ho, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nezich, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Son, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bulovic, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dresselhaus, M. Much research was focused on developing routes for obtaining large sheets of monolayer or bilayer graphene.  This was recently achieved by CVD of CH4 or C2H2 gases on copper or nickel substrates.  But CVD is limited to the use of gaseous raw materials, making it difficult to apply the technol. to a wider variety of potential feedstocks.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis and lithium storage properties of Co3O4 nanosheet-assembled multishelled hollow spheres</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xi; Wu, Xing-Long; Guo, Yu-Guo; Zhong, Yeteng; Cao, Xinqiang; Ma, Ying; Yao, Jiannian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Single-, double-, and triple-shelled hollow spheres assembled by Co3O4 nanosheets are successfully synthesized through a novel method.  The possible formation mechanism of these novel structures was investigated using powder X-ray diffraction, scanning and transmission electron microscopies, Fourier transform IR, XPS, and thermogravimetric anal.  Both poly(vinylpyrrolidone) (PVP) soft templates and the formation of cobalt glycolate play key roles in the formation of these novel multishelled hollow structures.  When tested as the anode material in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), these multishelled microspheres exhibit excellent cycling performance, good rate capacity, and enhanced lithium storage capacity.  This superior cyclic stability and capacity result from the synergetic effect of small diffusion lengths in the nanosheet building blocks and sufficient void space to buffer the vol. expansion.  This facile strategy may be extended to synthesize other transition metal oxide materials with hollow multishelled micro-/nanostrucutures, which may find application in sensors and catalysts due to their unique structural features.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp1uSDuUuefD7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhhz335Agb_Ig"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXmvVGktL8%253D&amp;md5=7e8d04e7ed751a3f5f18af7c9412d972</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcrysgro.2007.01.043"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ren, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Shape-Controlled Synthesis of Cu<sub>2</sub>O Nanocrystals Assisted by PVP and Application as Catalyst for Synthesis of Carbon Nanofibers</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Shape-controlled synthesis of Cu2O nanocrystals assisted by PVP and application as catalyst for synthesis of carbon nanofibers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Hui; Ren, Xue; Cui, Zuolin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Crystal Growth</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this paper, cuprous oxide (Cu2O) nanostructures with different shapes, such as spheres, cubes and rods, have been synthesized by reducing copper nitrate trihydrate with ethylene glycol in the present of poly(vinylpyrrolidone) (PVP).  The molar ratio of PVP (in the repeating unit)/Cu(NO3)2·3H2O and reaction temp. have significant effects on the formation and growth of these Cu2O nanostructures.  The Cu2O nanorods were fabricated at the molar ratios of PVP/Cu(NO3)2·3H2O 2-3, while spherical and cubic nanoparticles were formed at the ratios of PVP/Cu(NO3)2·3H2O 5-7 and 10-15. With the as-prepd. nanoparticles as catalyst, carbon nanofibers (CNFs) were synthesized by catalytic polymn. of acetylene at a lower temp. (250 °C).                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Uniform hollow Fe3O4 spheres prepared by template-free solvothermal method as anode material for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jingjing; Yao, Yu; Huang, Tao; Yu, Aishui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Unique hollow Fe3O4 spheres are prepd. by a simple template-free solvothermal reaction.  In the reaction, ethylene glycol and polyvinylpyrrolidone serve as the reducing agent and surface stabilizer, resp.  Ammonium acetate plays the role of the structure-directing agent, which combines with the Ostwald ripening process, resulting in the favored formation of hollow structures.  The morphologies and structures are characterized by x-ray diffraction, SEM, and transmission electron microscopy.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Formation of Uniform Fe3O4 Hollow Spheres Organized by Ultrathin Nanosheets and Their Excellent Lithium Storage Properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ma, Fei-Xiang; Hu, Han; Wu, Hao Bin; Xu, Cheng-Yan; Xu, Zhichuan; Zhen, Liang; Lou, Xiong Wen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, a facile solvothermal approach is developed combined with subsequent calcination to synthesize highly uniform hierarchical Fe3O4 hollow spheres, which are composed of ultrathin porous nanosheets.  One-pot solvothermal formation of hollow Fe-contg. precursor spheres is the key step in this work.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile Ultrasonic Synthesis of CoO Quantum Dot/Graphene Nanosheet Composites with High Lithium Storage Capacity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Peng, Chengxin; Chen, Bingdi; Qin, Yao; Yang, Shihe; Li, Chunzhong; Zuo, Yuanhui; Liu, Siyang; Yang, Jinhu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1074-1081</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report a facile ultrasonic method to synthesize well-dispersed CoO quantum dots (3-8 nm) on graphene nanosheets at room temp. by employing Co4(CO)12 as cobalt precursor.  The prepd. CoO/graphene composites displayed high performance as an anode material for lithium-ion battery, including high reversible lithium storage capacity (1592 mA-h/g after 50 cycles), high Coulombic efficiency (&gt;95%), excellent cycling stability, and high rate capability (1008 mA-h/g with a total retention of 77.6% after 50 cycles at a c.d. of 1000 mA/g, dramatically increased from the initial 50 mA/g).  The extraordinary performance arises from the structure advantages of the composites; the nanosized CoO quantum dots with high dispersity on conductive graphene substrates supply not only large quantity of accessible active sites for lithium ion insertion but also good cond. and short diffusion length for lithium ions, which are beneficial for high capacity and rate capability.  Meanwhile, the isolated CoO quantum dots anchored tightly on the graphene nanosheets can effectively circumvent the vol. expansion/contraction assocd. with lithium insertion/extn. during discharge/charge processes, which is good for high capacity as well as cycling stability.  Moreover, regarding the anomalous behavior of capacity increase with cycles (activation effect) obsd., we proposed a tentative hypothesis stressing the competition between the cond. increase and the amorphization of the composite electrodes during cycling in detg. the trends of the capacity, in the hope to gain a fuller understanding of the inner working of the novel nanostructured electrode-based lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxLbSlSmqRbLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhmwL3VO2F-7A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XktVKgsg%253D%253D&amp;md5=e8403e680ec193fee2711a798cb4ea85</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA04023F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tay, B.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ fabrication of three-dimensional, ultrathin graphite/carbon nanotube/NiO composite as binder-free electrode for high-performance energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Wenwen; Lu, Congxiang; Wang, Xingli; Liang, Kun; Tay, Beng Kang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">624-633</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal oxides have attracted considerable attention as promising electrode materials for energy storage, but the use of metal oxides for electrodes still faces challenges such as attaining high capacity, good cycle stability, and high-rated performance.  Therefore, rational design of electrode architectures and assembling metal oxides into desired structures to further enhance electrochem. performance is necessary.  Here, novel 3-dimensional electrode architectures consisting of 3-dimensional ultra-thin graphite film (UGF)/C nanotubes (CNTs) uniformly covered by NiO nanosheets are successfully constructed by a CVD and subsequent electrodeposition, which are directly used as bind-free electrodes for supercapacitors and Li-ion batteries.  In such composite structures, 3-dimensional UGF/CNTs serve as substrates for NiO nanosheet decoration, and act as spacers to stabilize the composite structure, making the active surfaces of NiO nanosheets accessible for electrolyte penetration and accommodating vol. changes during charge/discharge processes.  As expected, 3-dimensional UGF/CNTs/NiO as electrode material for supercapacitors showed high specific capacitance (750.8 F g-1 at c.d. of 1 A g-1), superior rate performance (capacitance of 575.6 F g-1 at 10 A g-1) and excellent cycle stability (no decay after 3000 cycles).  Also, the 3-dimensional CNTs/UGF/NiO composite also exhibited enhanced Li storage properties as anode materials for Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpEGNCM7mFPmrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhmwL3VO2F-7A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhsFOltLvF&amp;md5=c21ab9fe01c433dc0fb3b86133e073b5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1021/nn300098m"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, D.-W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yin, L.-C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, H.-M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Oxygen Bridges between NiO Nanosheets and Graphene for Improvement of Lithium Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2012</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">6</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3214</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">3223</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Oxygen Bridges between NiO Nanosheets and Graphene for Improvement of Lithium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Guangmin; Wang, Da-Wei; Yin, Li-Chang; Li, Na; Li, Feng; Cheng, Hui-Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3214-3223</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors report oxygen bridges between graphene with oxygen functional groups and NiO from anal. by XPS, Fourier transform IR spectroscopy, and Raman spectroscopy, and they also confirm the conformation of oxygen bridges by first-principles calcns.  NiO nanosheets (NiO NSs) are found to be bonded strongly to graphene through oxygen bridges.  The oxygen bridges mainly originate from the pinning of hydroxyl/epoxy groups from graphene on the Ni atoms of NiO NSs.  The calcd. adsorption energies (1.37 and 1.84 eV for graphene with hydroxyl and epoxy) of a Ni adatom on oxygenated graphene by binding with oxygen are comparable with that on graphene (1.26 eV).  However, the calcd. diffusion barriers of the Ni adatom on the oxygenated graphene surface (2.23 and 1.69 eV for graphene with hydroxyl and epoxy) are much larger than that on the graphene (0.19 eV).  Therefore, the NiO NS is anchored strongly on the graphene through a C-O-Ni bridge, which allows a high reversible capacity and excellent rate performance.  The easy binding/difficult dissocg. characteristic of Ni adatoms on the oxygenated graphene facilitates fast electron hopping from graphene to NiO and thus the reversible lithiation and delithiation of NiO.  The understanding of this oxygen bridge between graphene and NiO will lead to the development of other high-performance electrode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr26TL2YHdDibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhmwL3VO2F-7A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XktVGgtrg%253D&amp;md5=eebb442a11e7461631544aff9b18c88c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2014.06.022"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Si, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Deng, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xi, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Schmidt, O.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Multifunctional Ni/NiO hybrid nanomembranes as anode materials for high-rate Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Xiaolei; Si, Wenping; Liu, Xianghong; Deng, Junwen; Xi, Lixia; Liu, Lifeng; Yan, Chenglin; Schmidt, Oliver G.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

                        cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Preparation of 3D flower-like NiO hierarchical architectures and their electrochemical properties in lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Qing; Chen, Yuejiao; Yang, Ting; Lei, Danni; Zhang, Guanhua; Mei, Lin; Chen, Libao; Li, Qiuhong; Wang, Taihong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Three-dimensional (3D) flower-like NiO hierarchical architectures have been synthesized by a simple ethanolamine-mediated self-assembly route and subsequent calcination process.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hierarchically porous materials are an ideal material platform for constructing high performance Li-ion batteries (LIBs), offering great advantages such as large contact area between the electrode and the electrolyte, fast and flexible transport pathways for the electrolyte ions and the space for buffering the strain caused by repeated Li insertion/extn.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are attracting considerable attention with expectation of replacing lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) in large-scale energy storage systems (ESSs).  To explore high performance anode materials for SIBs is highly desired subject to the current anode research mainly limited to carbonaceous materials.  In this study, a series of transition metal oxides (TMOs) is successfully demonstrated as anodes for SIBs for the first time.  The sodium uptake/ext. is confirmed in the way of reversible conversion reaction.  The pseudocapacitance-type behavior is also obsd. in the contribution of sodium capacity.                         cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Micro-nanostructured CuO/C spheres as high-performance anode materials for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Yanying; Zhang, Ning; Zhao, Qing; Liang, Jing; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this paper, we report on the synthesis of micro-nanostructured CuO/C spheres by aerosol spray pyrolysis and their application as high-performance anodes in sodium-ion batteries.  Micro-nanostructured CuO/C spheres with different CuO contents were synthesized through aerosol spray pyrolysis by adjusting the ratio of reactants and heat-treated by an oxidn. process.  The as-prepd. CuO/C spheres show uniformly spherical morphol., in which CuO nanoparticles (∼10 nm) are homogeneously embedded in the carbon matrix (denoted as 10-CuO/C).  The electrochem. performance of 10-CuO/C with a carbon wt. of 44% was evaluated as the anode material for Na-ion batteries.  It can deliver a capacity of 402 mA h g-1 after 600 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1.  Furthermore, a capacity of 304 mA h g-1 was obtained at a high c.d. of 2000 mA g-1.  The superior electrochem. performance of the micro-nanostructured CuO/C spheres leads to the enhancement of the electronic cond. of the nanocomposite and the accommodation of the vol. variation of CuO/C during charge/discharge cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo5WWNUfJdthLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifakq-vchwKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitFOrt7jK&amp;md5=3d31a9ea531c3058bd5224af59f51e37</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201303702"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Su, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Mesoporous SnO Microspheres as High Capacity Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem. - Eur.                         cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical Mesoporous SnO Microspheres as High Capacity Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Su, Dawei; Xie, Xiuqiang; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">20</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3192-3197</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CEUJED</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Mesoporous SnO microspheres were synthesized by a hydrothermal method using NaSO4 as the morphol. directing agent.  Field emission SEM (FESEM), transmission electron microscopy (TEM) and high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM) analyses showed that SnO microspheres consist of nanosheets with a thickness of about 20 nm.  Each nanosheet contains a mesoporous structure with a pore size of approx. 5 nm.  When applied as anode materials in Na-ion batteries, SnO microspheres exhibited high reversible sodium storage capacity, good cyclability and a satisfactory high rate performance.  Through ex situ XRD anal., it was found that Na+ ions first insert themselves into SnO crystals, and then react with SnO to generate cryst. Sn, followed by Na-Sn alloying with the formation of cryst. NaSn2 phase.  During the charge process, there are two slopes corresponding to the de-alloying of Na-Sn compds. and oxidization of Sn, resp.  The high sodium storage capacity and good electrochem. performance could be ascribed to the unique hierarchical mesoporous architecture of SnO microspheres.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrXdrhnu8DXbLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lifakq-vchwKA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXisFWiu78%253D&amp;md5=744dcb004cf9eba80fc40d876769c221</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201401123"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">3D Porous γ-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C Nanocomposite as High-Performance Anode Material of Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. class="paneContainer"><ul class="rlist tab__content" tabindex="0"><li id="pane-m1" aria-labelledby="pane-m1" class="tab__pane tab__pane-figures active"><figure data-id="f_tgr1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Abstract</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#f_tgr1"><img class="rightTab-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/medium/nn-2015-05041r_0008.gif" alt="" id="rightTab-tgr1"></a><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/large/nn-2015-05041r_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.5b05041&amp;id=f_tgr1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure data-id="sch1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Scheme 1</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#sch1"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/medium/nn-2015-05041r_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/large/nn-2015-05041r_0007.jpeg" id="rightTab-gr1" class="rightTab-fig internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><div class="title2">Scheme 1. Schematic Illustration of the Formation of NiO/Ni/Graphene Composites<sup>a</sup></div></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/large/nn-2015-05041r_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.5b05041&amp;id=sch1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div><p class="last"></p><p class="last"><span class="fn-label">Scheme a</span>The Ni-MOF possesses a hollow, ball-in-ball structure with needles on the surface. After the first thermal annealing in N<sub>2</sub>, MOFs were converted into Ni/Graphene composite. After the second thermal annealing in air, NiO/Ni/Graphene composites were obtained. The resulting composites have the same hollow, ball-in-ball structure as their MOF precursor.</p><p></p></figure><figure data-id="fig1" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#fig1"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/medium/nn-2015-05041r_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/large/nn-2015-05041r_0002.jpeg" id="rightTab-gr2" class="rightTab-fig internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. Formation of hierarchical, hollow, ball-in-ball Ni-MOFs. (a, b) SEM images of Ni-MOFs prepared with reaction time of 10 h (scale bar: 10 μm for (a) and 500 nm for (b)). (c–e) TEM images of Ni-MOFs prepared with reaction time of (c) 3 h; (d) 5 h; (e) and 10 h (Scale bar: 1 μm). The Ni-MOFs are smooth solid balls at the beginning. They became hollow with extended reaction time. (f–h) XRD patterns of Ni-MOFs obtained with reaction time of (f) 3 h; (g) 5 h; and (h) 10 h. (i) The scheme illustrates the mechanism of structure evolution: the amorphous materials inside the sphere were dissolved and diffused to the surface, forming the needle-like structures by crystallization and generating the voids inside the sphere.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/large/nn-2015-05041r_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.5b05041&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure data-id="fig2" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#fig2"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/medium/nn-2015-05041r_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/large/nn-2015-05041r_0003.jpeg" id="rightTab-gr3" class="rightTab-fig internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. Characterization of annealed Ni-MOFs. (a,b) SEM images of product obtained after annealing Ni-MOF at 450 °C for 30 min in N<sub>2</sub>. (c) XRD pattern confirmed the formation of metallic Ni phase. (d, e) SEM images and corresponding XRD pattern (f) of NiO/Ni/Graphene composite obtained with a second-step annealing process in air at 200 °C for 30 min (scale bar: 10 μm for a and d, 500 nm for b and e).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/large/nn-2015-05041r_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.5b05041&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure data-id="fig3" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#fig3"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/medium/nn-2015-05041r_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/large/nn-2015-05041r_0004.jpeg" id="rightTab-gr4" class="rightTab-fig internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. (a) TEM image (scale bar: 200 nm) reveals the NiO/Ni/Graphene sphere has a hollow structure. The diameter is about 1.5 μm which is in accordance with the SEM observation. (b) SAED pattern (scale bar: 2 1/nm) shows a group of diffraction rings which are indexed to the (200), (111), (220) of NiO and (111) of Ni. (c) HRTEM image (scale bar: 5 nm) was taken from a single needle grown on the surface of sphere, showing the NiO/Ni nanocrystals with an average size of ∼5 nm. (d) HRTEM image (scale bar: 2 nm) was taken from the edge of the needle, showing a carbon coating with layered structure. (e) HRTEM image (scale bar: 2 nm) reveals that the <i>d</i>-spacing of the cubic NiO (200) plane is 2.1 Å. (f) STEM <i>Z</i>-contrast image and the corresponding elemental EDX mapping images of (g) nickel, (h) oxygen, and (i) carbon (scale bar: 500 nm) indicated that every element was homogeneously distributed.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/large/nn-2015-05041r_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.5b05041&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure data-id="fig4" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#fig4"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/medium/nn-2015-05041r_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/large/nn-2015-05041r_0005.jpeg" id="rightTab-gr5" class="rightTab-fig internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. Electrochemical performance of NiO/Ni/Graphene composite for LIBs: (a) Cyclic voltammogram of NiO/Ni/Graphene composite collected at a scan rate of 0.2 mV/s within the voltage range of 0.005–3 V. (b) Galvanostatic charge and discharge profiles for the 1st and 2nd cycles at a current density of 200 mA/g and 1st, 200th, 500th, and 1000th cycles at a current density of 2 A/g. (c) Cycle performance at a current density of 2 A/g (200 mA/g was used for activation at first 5 cycles); the NiO/Ni/Graphene can maintain a specific capacity up to 962 mAh/g even after 1000 cycles. (d) Specific capacities at current densities ranging from 200 mA/g to 15 A/g. An average specific capacity of 805 mA/g was achieved at 15 A/g. (e) Ratability comparison between our work and previous results. The NiO/Ni/Graphene nanocomposite in this work exhibited better ratability than previous reports of NiO based electrode.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/large/nn-2015-05041r_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.5b05041&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure data-id="fig5" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#fig5"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/medium/nn-2015-05041r_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/large/nn-2015-05041r_0006.jpeg" id="rightTab-gr6" class="rightTab-fig internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. Electrochemical performance of NiO/Ni/Graphene composite for SIBs: (a) Cyclic voltammogram of NiO/Ni/Graphene composite collected at a scan rate of 0.2 mV/s within the voltage range of 0.005–3 V. (b) Galvanostatic charge and discharge profiles for the 1st and 2nd cycles at a current density of 200 mA/g and 1st, 10th, 100th and 200th cycles at a current density of 1 A/g. (c) Cycle performance of SIBs at a current density of 1 A/g (200 mA/g was used for activation in the first 5 cycles) indicated that the fading rate was 0.2% per cycle. (d) Specific capacities at current densities range from 200 mA/g to 2 A/g. An average specific capacity of 207 mAh/g was achieved at 2 A/g.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.5b05041/asset/images/large/nn-2015-05041r_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.5b05041&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></li><li id="pane-m2" aria-labelledby="pane-m2" class="tab__pane tab__pane-references"><div class="refs-header-label"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i12">References</h2></div></div></div><hr></div><p class="rightTab-references-count">

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The increasing interest in energy storage for the grid can be attributed to multiple factors, including the capital costs of managing peak demands, the investments needed for grid reliability, and the integration of renewable energy sources.  Although existing energy storage is dominated by pumped hydroelec., there is the recognition that battery systems can offer a no. of high-value opportunities, provided that lower costs can be obtained.  The battery systems reviewed here include sodium-sulfur batteries that are com. available for grid applications, redox-flow batteries that offer low cost, and lithium-ion batteries whose development for com. electronics and elec. vehicles is being applied to grid storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrZwDymuubZm7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhC-ltmcwxCVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhsVGktL%252FJ&amp;md5=5035bfda7631ad9d075e8836e61146ef</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201202623"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xia, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Reconstruction of Conformal Nanoscale MnO on Graphene as a High-Capacity and Long-Life Anode Material for Lithium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reconstruction of Conformal Nanoscale MnO on Graphene as a High-Capacity and Long-Life Anode Material for Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Yongming; Hu, Xianluo; Luo, Wei; Xia, Fangfang; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To tackle the issue of inferior cycle stability and rate capability for MnO anode materials in lithium ion batteries, a facile strategy is explored to prep. a hybrid material consisting of MnO nanocrystals grown on conductive graphene nanosheets.  The prepd. MnO/graphene hybrid anode exhibits a reversible capacity as high as 2014.1 mAh g-1 after 150 discharge/charge cycles at 200 mA g-1, excellent rate capability (625.8 mAh g-1 at 3000 mA g-1), and superior cyclability (843.3 mAh g-1 even after 400 discharge/charge cycles at 2000 mA g-1 with only 0.01% capacity loss per cycle).  The results suggest that the reconstruction of the MnO/graphene electrodes is intrinsic due to conversion reactions.  A long-term stable nanoarchitecture of graphene-supported ultrafine manganese oxide nanoparticles is formed upon cycling, which yields a long-life anode material for lithium ion batteries.  The lithiation and delithiation behavior suggests that the further oxidn. of Mn(II) to Mn(IV) and the interfacial lithium storage upon cycling contribute to the enhanced specific capacity.  The excellent rate capability benefits from the presence of conductive graphene and a short transportation length for both lithium ions and electrons.  Moreover, the as-formed hybrid nanostructure of MnO on graphene may help achieve faster kinetics of conversion reactions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqSjyTOe_ODXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhC-ltmcwxCVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhvVWnsL%252FE&amp;md5=993266e37afcdc7949e8735381125094</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1021/nn401059h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">He, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shi, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon-encapsulated Fe<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Nanoparticles as a High-rate Lithium Ion Battery Anode Material</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">4459</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">4469</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-Encapsulated Fe3O4 Nanoparticles as a High-Rate Lithium Ion Battery Anode Material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Chunnian; Wu, Shan; Zhao, Naiqin; Shi, Chunsheng; Liu, Enzuo; Li, Jiajun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4459-4469</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile and scalable in situ synthesis strategy is developed to fabricate carbon-encapsulated Fe3O4 nanoparticles homogeneously embedded in two-dimensional (2D) porous graphitic carbon nanosheets (Fe3O4@C@PGC nanosheets) as a durable high-rate lithium-ion battery anode material.  With assistance of the surface of NaCl particles, 2D Fe@C@PGC nanosheets can be in situ synthesized by using the Fe(NO3)3·9H2O and C6H12O6 as the metal and carbon precursor, resp.  After annealing under air, the Fe@C@PGC nanosheets can be converted to Fe3O4@C@PGC nanosheets, in which Fe3O4 nanoparticles (∼18.2 nm) coated with conformal and thin onion-like carbon shells are homogeneously embedded in 2D high-conducting carbon nanosheets with a thickness of &lt;30 nm.  In the constructed architecture, the thin carbon shells can avoid the direct exposure of encapsulated Fe3O4 to the electrolyte and preserve the structural and interfacial stabilization of Fe3O4 nanoparticles.  Meanwhile, the flexible and conductive PGC nanosheets can accommodate the mech. stress induced by the vol. change of embedded Fe3O4@C nanoparticles as well as inhibit the aggregation of Fe3O4 nanoparticles and thus maintain the structural and elec. integrity of the Fe3O4@C@PGC electrode during the lithiation/delithiation processes.  As a result, this Fe3O4@C@PGC electrode exhibits superhigh rate capability (858, 587, and 311 mA-h/g at 5C, 10C, and 20C, resp., 1C = 1 A/g) and extremely excellent cycling performance at high rates (only 3.47% capacity loss after 350 cycles at a high rate of 10C), which is the best one ever reported for a Fe3O4-based electrode including various nanostructured Fe3O4 anode materials, composite electrodes, etc.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoP9hXexjGQwLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhC-ltmcwxCVg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXmtlersrY%253D&amp;md5=88c26678ee82d2142bfa61ddbc0aa8e1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201401421"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">3D Hierarchical Porous α-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Nanosheets for High-Performance Lithium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review of recent advances in strategies for advanced metal oxide-based hybrid nanostructure design, with the focus on the binder-free film/array electrodes.  Metal oxide nanostructures are promising electrode materials for lithium-ion batteries and supercapacitors because of their high specific capacity/capacitance, typically 2-3 times higher than that of the carbon/graphite-based materials.  These binder-free electrodes, with the integration of unique merits of each component, can provide larger electrochem. active surface area, faster electron transport and superior ion diffusion, thus leading to substantially improved cycling and rate performance.  However, their cycling stability and rate performance still cannot meet the requirements of practical applications.  Several recently emerged concepts of using ordered nanostructure arrays, synergetic core-shell structures, nanostructured current collectors, and flexible paper/textile electrodes are highlighted, pointing out advantages and challenges where appropriate.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  High-energy consumption in our day-to-day life can be balanced not only by harvesting pollution-free renewable energy sources, but also requires proper storage and distribution of energy.  In this regard, lithium ion batteries are currently considered as effective energy storage devices and involve the most active research.  There exist several review articles dealing with various sections of LIBs, such as the anode, the cathode, electrolytes, electrode-electrolyte interface, etc.  However, the anode is considered to be a crucial component affecting the performance of LIBs as evident from the tremendous amt. of current research work carried out in this area. Different types of anode materials, such as carbon-based materials, alloys, Si-based materials, transition metal oxides, and transition metal chalcogenides, with their unique phys. and electrochem. properties, are discussed.  Various approaches to designing materials in the form of 0, 1, and 2D nanostructures and their effect of size and morphol. on their performance as anode materials in LIBs are reviewed.  Moreover, the article emphasizes smart approaches for making core-shell particles, nanoheterostructures, nanocomposites or nanohybrids with the combination of electrochem. active materials and conductive carbonaceous or electrochem. inactive materials to achieve LIBs with high capacity, high rate capability, and excellent cycling stability. Nanostructured materials such as nano-carbons, alloys, metal oxides, and metal sulfides/nitrides have been used as anodes for next-generation LIBs with high reversible capacity, fast power capability, good safety, and long cycle life.  This is due to their relatively short mass and charge pathways, high transport rates of both lithium ions and electrons, and other extremely charming surface activities. The major goals of this review are to give a broad overview of recent scientific researches and developments of anode materials using novel nanoscience and nanotechnol. and to highlight new progresses in using these nanostructured materials to develop high-performance LIBs.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Origins of the irreversible capacity loss were addressed through probing changes in the electronic and structural properties of hollow-structured Co3O4 nanoparticles (NPs) during lithiation and delithiation using electrochem. Co3O4 transistor devices that function as a Co3O4 Li-ion battery.  Additive-free Co3O4 NPs were assembled into a Li-ion battery, allowing us to isolate and explore the effects of the Co and Li2O formation/decompn. conversion reactions on the elec. and structural degrdn. within Co3O4 NP films.  NP films ranging between a single monolayer and multilayered film hundreds of nanometers thick prepd. with blade-coating and electrophoretic deposition methods, resp., were embedded in the transistor devices for in situ conduction measurements as a function of battery cycles.  During battery operation, the electronic and structural properties of Co3O4 NP films in the bulk, Co3O4/electrolyte, and Co3O4/current collector interfaces were spatially mapped to address the origin of the initial irreversible capacity loss from the first lithiation process.  Further, change in carrier injection/extn. between the current collector and the Co3O4 NPs was explored using a modified electrochem. transistor device with multiple voltage probes along the elec. channel.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqeW1qjRDLaJrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0likqxUVmU2DJg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXpt1Kqs78%253D&amp;md5=7e7aecd835edf14d76d4ffc5bfe633a4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201204588"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zou, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xia, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qie, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Microwave-Induced <i>in situ</i> Synthesis of Zn<sub>2</sub>GeO<sub>4</sub>/N-doped Graphene Nanocomposites and Their Lithium-Storage Properties</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem. - Eur.                         rightTab-cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Microwave-Induced In Situ Synthesis of Zn2GeO4/N-Doped Graphene Nanocomposites and Their Lithium-Storage Properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zou, Feng; Hu, Xianluo; Sun, Yongming; Luo, Wei; Xia, Fangfang; Long, Qie; Jiang, Yan; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">19</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CEUJED</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Zn2GeO4/N-doped graphene nanocomposites were synthesized through a fast microwave-assisted route on a large scale.  The resulting nanohybrids are comprised of Zn2GeO4 nanorods that are well-embedded in N-doped graphene sheets by in situ reducing and doping.  Importantly, the N-doped graphene sheets serve as elastic networks to disperse and elec. wire together the Zn2GeO4 nanorods, thereby effectively relieving the vol.-expansion/contraction and aggregation of the nanoparticles during charge and discharge processes.  We demonstrate that an electrode that is made of the as-formed Zn2GeO4/N-doped graphene nanocomposite exhibits high capacity (1463 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1), good cyclability, and excellent rate capability (531 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 3200 mA g-1).  Its superior lithium-storage performance could be related to a synergistic effect of the unique nanostructured hybrid, in which the Zn2GeO4 nanorods are well-stabilized by the high electronic conduction and flexibility of N-doped graphene sheets.  This work offers an effective strategy for the fabrication of functionalized ternary-oxide-based composites as high-performance electrode materials that involve structural conversion and transformation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpm7DQDJ59d87Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0likqxUVmU2DJg"> &gt;&gt;                         rightTab-cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis of sandwiched Zn2GeO4-graphene oxide nanocomposite as a stable and high-capacity anode for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zou, Feng; Hu, Xianluo; Long, Qie; Jiang, Yan; Xiong, Xiaoqin; Qiao, Yun; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Traditional metal anode materials in lithium-ion batteries are plagued by instability upon discharge-charge cycling.  We report that a unique sandwiched Zn2GeO4-graphene oxide nanocomposite has been synthesized on a large scale through a simple ion-exchange reaction, whereby Zn2GeO4 nanorods with lengths of 600 nm and widths of 40 nm are homogeneously sandwiched into the graphene oxide matrix.  Compared with bare Zn2GeO4 nanorods, a dramatic improvement in the electrochem. performance of the resulting nanocomposite has been achieved.  In the voltage window of 0.001-3 V, the electrode of the Zn2GeO4-graphene oxide nanocomposite delivers a specific capacity as high as 1150 mA h g-1 at 200 mA g-1 after 100 discharge-charge cycles.  Even at a high c.d. of 3.2 A g-1, a capacity of 522 mA h g-1 can be retained.  The unusual electrochem. performance including highly reversible capacity and excellent rate capability arise from synergetic chem. coupling effects between Zn2GeO4 and graphene oxide.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrIkg4tVvn4abVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0likqxUVmU2DJg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvFOjs7nF&amp;md5=034e87ef9c04dc22a079b1c2f34a6fe1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref17" class="rightTabRefNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit17" data-doi="10.1039/C1EE02831F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luan, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Madhavi, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lou, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Recent progress on graphene/metal oxide composites as advanced electrode materials in lithium ion batteries (LIBs) and electrochem. capacitors (ECs) is described, highlighting the importance of synergistic effects between graphene and metal oxides and the beneficial role of graphene in composites for LIBs and ECs.  It is demonstrated that, when the composites are used as electrode materials for LIBs and ECs, compared to their individual constituents, graphene/metal oxide composites with unique structural variables such as anchored, wrapped, encapsulated, sandwich, layered and mixed models have a significant improvement in their electrochem. properties such as high capacity, high rate capability and excellent cycling stability.  First, an introduction on the properties, synthesis strategies and use of graphene is briefly given, followed by a state-of-the-art review on the prepn. of graphene/metal oxide composites and their electrochem. properties in LIBs and ECs.  Finally, the prospects and future challenges of graphene/metal oxide composites for energy storage are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpeqIWgkryT1LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhnmA-zyZ45lQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXisF2qtLY%253D&amp;md5=a2325f232a3c46fbba2275635984ad56</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201302710"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jeong, J. ZnO nanoarray-based electrode prepd. by growing ZnO@ZnO QDs/C core-shell nanorod arrays (NRAs) on flexible carbon cloth (CC).  Applied as anode material, the as-synthesized ZnO@ZnO QDs/C core-shell NRAs manifested high specific capacity and excellent cycling performance.  The self-supported ZnO@ZnO QDs/C NRAs exhibited a remarkable rate capability (a reversible capability of 1053, 913, 762, 591, and 530 mA-h g-1 at 100, 200, 400, 800, and 1000 mA g-1, resp.) and as well as remarkable cycling performance (approx. 11% capacity loss after 100 cycles at 500 mA g-1 with, a capacity retention of 699 mA-h g-1).         </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel porous ZnO/ZnFe2O4/C octahedra with hollow interiors is fabricated using metal-org. frameworks (MOF) as both the precursor and the self-sacrificing template. The strategy is easy, tunable, and cost-effective, and therefore it is highly promising for mass prodn.  Ultrafine ZnO and ZnFe2O4 nanocrystals of &lt; 5 nm are generated during thermal annealing of hollow MOF-5 octahedra, and these nanocrystals are simultaneously embedded in a 3D inter-connected, porous carbon framework derived from in-situ carbonization of the org. ligands.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Material design in terms of their morphologies other than solid nanoparticles can lead to more advanced properties.  At the example of Fe oxide, the authors explored the electrochem. properties of hollow nanoparticles with an application as a cathode and anode.  Such nanoparticles contain very high concn. of cation vacancies that can be efficiently used for reversible Li ion intercalation without structural change.  Cycling in high voltage range results in high capacity (∼132 mA-h/g at 2.5 V), 99.7% Coulombic efficiency, superior rate performance (133 mA-h/g at 3000 mA/g) and excellent stability (no fading at fast rate during &gt;500 cycles).  Cation vacancies in hollow Fe oxide nanoparticles also are responsible for the enhanced capacity in the conversion reactions.
