        </div><div class="casAbstract">Problems assocd. with large-scale pattern growth of graphene constitute one of the main obstacles to using this material in device applications.  Recently, macroscopic-scale graphene films were prepd. by two-dimensional assembly of graphene sheets chem. derived from graphite crystals and graphene oxides.  However, the sheet resistance of these films was found to be much larger than theor. expected values.  Here we report the direct synthesis of large-scale graphene films using chem. vapor deposition on thin nickel layers, and present two different methods of patterning the films and transferring them to arbitrary substrates.  The transferred graphene films show very low sheet resistance of ∼280 Ω per square, with ∼80% optical transparency.  At low temps., the monolayers transferred to silicon dioxide substrates show electron mobility greater than 3,700 cm2 V-1 s-1 and exhibit the half-integer quantum Hall effect, implying that the quality of graphene grown by chem. vapor deposition is as high as mech. cleaved graphene.  Employing the outstanding mech. properties of graphene, we also demonstrate the macroscopic use of these highly conducting and transparent electrodes in flexible, stretchable, foldable electronics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqKGOlTbW4cmrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh5M0uaWPyvVA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1MXht1ehtL4%253D&amp;md5=0eef5b83d20b2e74add31eb1aa19337e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1021/nl801827v"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Reina, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jia, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ho, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nezich, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Son, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bulovic, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dresselhaus, M. The Cu2O nanorods were fabricated at the molar ratios of PVP/Cu(NO3)2·3H2O 2-3, while spherical and cubic nanoparticles were formed at the ratios of PVP/Cu(NO3)2·3H2O 5-7 and 10-15.  Increasing with reaction temps., monodisperse particles were obtained.  The as-synthesized nanoparticles and nanorods were investigated by transmission electron microscopy (TEM), and field emission SEM (FE-SEM) and X-ray diffractometry (XRD).  With the as-prepd. nanoparticles as catalyst, carbon nanofibers (CNFs) were synthesized by catalytic polymn. of acetylene at a lower temp. (250 °C).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Unique hollow Fe3O4 spheres are prepd. by a simple template-free solvothermal reaction.  In the reaction, ethylene glycol and polyvinylpyrrolidone serve as the reducing agent and surface stabilizer, resp.  Ammonium acetate plays the role of the structure-directing agent, which combines with the Ostwald ripening process, resulting in the favored formation of hollow structures.  The morphologies and structures are characterized by x-ray diffraction, SEM, and transmission electron microscopy.  The hollow Fe3O4 spheres exhibit excellent cycling and rate performance as anode material for lithium-ion batteries, delivering reversible sp. capacities of 870 mA-h/g even after 50 cycles at 100 mA/g and 836 mA-h/g at 500 mA/g.  The excellent electrochem. performance can be attributed to their hollow nanostructure and excellent structural stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqnRhvRShuR_7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgrrZzQ4vmExA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhtFSisr3F&amp;md5=bedeb315aa6021613a2068e74be6256e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201501130"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ma, F.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We report a facile ultrasonic method to synthesize well-dispersed CoO quantum dots (3-8 nm) on graphene nanosheets at room temp. by employing Co4(CO)12 as cobalt precursor.  The prepd. CoO/graphene composites displayed high performance as an anode material for lithium-ion battery, including high reversible lithium storage capacity (1592 mA-h/g after 50 cycles), high Coulombic efficiency (&gt;95%), excellent cycling stability, and high rate capability (1008 mA-h/g with a total retention of 77.6% after 50 cycles at a c.d. of 1000 mA/g, dramatically increased from the initial 50 mA/g).  The extraordinary performance arises from the structure advantages of the composites; the nanosized CoO quantum dots with high dispersity on conductive graphene substrates supply not only large quantity of accessible active sites for lithium ion insertion but also good cond. and short diffusion length for lithium ions, which are beneficial for high capacity and rate capability.  Meanwhile, the isolated CoO quantum dots anchored tightly on the graphene nanosheets can effectively circumvent the vol. expansion/contraction assocd. with lithium insertion/extn. during discharge/charge processes, which is good for high capacity as well as cycling stability.  Moreover, regarding the anomalous behavior of capacity increase with cycles (activation effect) obsd., we proposed a tentative hypothesis stressing the competition between the cond. increase and the amorphization of the composite electrodes during cycling in detg. the trends of the capacity, in the hope to gain a fuller understanding of the inner working of the novel nanostructured electrode-based lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrxLbSlSmqRbLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj_GnOsAL01Qg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XktVKgsg%253D%253D&amp;md5=e8403e680ec193fee2711a798cb4ea85</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref44" class="rightTabRefNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit44" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA04023F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tay, B.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal oxides have attracted considerable attention as promising electrode materials for energy storage, but the use of metal oxides for electrodes still faces challenges such as attaining high capacity, good cycle stability, and high-rated performance.  Therefore, rational design of electrode architectures and assembling metal oxides into desired structures to further enhance electrochem. performance is necessary.  Here, novel 3-dimensional electrode architectures consisting of 3-dimensional ultra-thin graphite film (UGF)/C nanotubes (CNTs) uniformly covered by NiO nanosheets are successfully constructed by a CVD and subsequent electrodeposition, which are directly used as bind-free electrodes for supercapacitors and Li-ion batteries.  In such composite structures, 3-dimensional UGF/CNTs serve as substrates for NiO nanosheet decoration, and act as spacers to stabilize the composite structure, making the active surfaces of NiO nanosheets accessible for electrolyte penetration and accommodating vol. changes during charge/discharge processes.  As expected, 3-dimensional UGF/CNTs/NiO as electrode material for supercapacitors showed high specific capacitance (750.8 F g-1 at c.d. of 1 A g-1), superior rate performance (capacitance of 575.6 F g-1 at 10 A g-1) and excellent cycle stability (no decay after 3000 cycles).                         rightTab-cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Oxygen Bridges between NiO Nanosheets and Graphene for Improvement of Lithium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Guangmin; Wang, Da-Wei; Yin, Li-Chang; Li, Na; Li, Feng; Cheng, Hui-Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors report oxygen bridges between graphene with oxygen functional groups and NiO from anal. by XPS, Fourier transform IR spectroscopy, and Raman spectroscopy, and they also confirm the conformation of oxygen bridges by first-principles calcns.  NiO nanosheets (NiO NSs) are found to be bonded strongly to graphene through oxygen bridges.  The oxygen bridges mainly originate from the pinning of hydroxyl/epoxy groups from graphene on the Ni atoms of NiO NSs.  The calcd. adsorption energies (1.37 and 1.84 eV for graphene with hydroxyl and epoxy) of a Ni adatom on oxygenated graphene by binding with oxygen are comparable with that on graphene (1.26 eV).  However, the calcd. diffusion barriers of the Ni adatom on the oxygenated graphene surface (2.23 and 1.69 eV for graphene with hydroxyl and epoxy) are much larger than that on the graphene (0.19 eV).  Therefore, the NiO NS is anchored strongly on the graphene through a C-O-Ni bridge, which allows a high reversible capacity and excellent rate performance.  The easy binding/difficult dissocg. characteristic of Ni adatoms on the oxygenated graphene facilitates fast electron hopping from graphene to NiO and thus the reversible lithiation and delithiation of NiO.  The understanding of this oxygen bridge between graphene and NiO will lead to the development of other high-performance electrode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr26TL2YHdDibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgJ89_xRro7wQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XktVGgtrg%253D&amp;md5=eebb442a11e7461631544aff9b18c88c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref46" class="rightTabRefNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2014.06.022"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Si, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Deng, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xi, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Schmidt, O.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Monodispersed hierarchical Co3O4 spheres with a uniform particle size distribution were intertwined with carbon nanotubes to form a (Co3O4@CNTs) composite.  The composite shows excellent cycling and rate performance with a capacity of up to 230 and 184 mA-h/g at currents of 1600 and 3200 mA/g, resp., which is likely attributed to the formation of mixed conducting networks of both Na+ ions and electrons.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrMzMKzES6j87Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgJ89_xRro7wQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtVKmu7zF&amp;md5=eb8de74b51868cd204d087867464c37b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref51" class="rightTabRefNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit51" data-doi="10.1039/C3CC47977C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jian, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shi, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> Nanocrystals Anchored onto Graphene Nanosheets as the Anode Material for Low-Cost Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Fe2O3 nanocrystals were uniformly anchored onto graphene nanosheets (Fe2O3@GNS) by a nanocasting technique, and the resulting composites were used as anodes for sodium-ion batteries.                 10.1016/j.nanoen.2014.02.002</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Transition metal oxides for high performance sodium ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jiang, Yinzhu; Hu, Meijuan; Zhang, Dan; Yuan, Tianzhi; Sun, Wenping; Xu, Ben; Yan, Mi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">60-66</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are attracting considerable attention with expectation of replacing lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) in large-scale energy storage systems (ESSs).  To explore high performance anode materials for SIBs is highly desired subject to the current anode research mainly limited to carbonaceous materials.  In this study, a series of transition metal oxides (TMOs) is successfully demonstrated as anodes for SIBs for the first time.  The sodium uptake/ext. is confirmed in the way of reversible conversion reaction.  The pseudocapacitance-type behavior is also obsd. in the contribution of sodium capacity.  For Fe2O3 anode, a reversible capacity of 386 mAh g-1at 100 mA g-1 is achieved over 200 cycles; as high as 233 mAh g-1is sustained even cycling at a large current-d. of 5 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGroiHe5VWwLV7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljpEJxaYHLOGg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXovVagtLk%253D&amp;md5=e05625359dabc9140c5026b3f39cc439</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref53" class="rightTabRefNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit53" data-doi="10.1039/C4NR06432A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Micro-Nanostructured CuO/C Spheres as High-Performance Anode Materials for Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2770</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">2776</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C4NR06432A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Micro-nanostructured CuO/C spheres as high-performance anode materials for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Yanying; Zhang, Ning; Zhao, Qing; Liang, Jing; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2770-2776</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2040-3372</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this paper, we report on the synthesis of micro-nanostructured CuO/C spheres by aerosol spray pyrolysis and their application as high-performance anodes in sodium-ion batteries.  Micro-nanostructured CuO/C spheres with different CuO contents were synthesized through aerosol spray pyrolysis by adjusting the ratio of reactants and heat-treated by an oxidn. process.  The as-prepd. CuO/C spheres show uniformly spherical morphol., in which CuO nanoparticles (∼10 nm) are homogeneously embedded in the carbon matrix (denoted as 10-CuO/C).  The electrochem. performance of 10-CuO/C with a carbon wt. of 44% was evaluated as the anode material for Na-ion batteries.  It can deliver a capacity of 402 mA h g-1 after 600 cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1.  Furthermore, a capacity of 304 mA h g-1 was obtained at a high c.d. of 2000 mA g-1.  The superior electrochem. performance of the micro-nanostructured CuO/C spheres leads to the enhancement of the electronic cond. of the nanocomposite and the accommodation of the vol. variation of CuO/C during charge/discharge cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo5WWNUfJdthLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljpEJxaYHLOGg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitFOrt7jK&amp;md5=3d31a9ea531c3058bd5224af59f51e37</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref54" class="rightTabRefNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit54" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201303702"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Su, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Mesoporous SnO Microspheres as High Capacity Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem. - Eur. J.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">20</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3192</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">3197</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/chem.201303702</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical Mesoporous SnO Microspheres as High Capacity Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Su, Dawei; Xie, Xiuqiang; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">20</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3192-3197</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CEUJED</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0947-6539</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Mesoporous SnO microspheres were synthesized by a hydrothermal method using NaSO4 as the morphol. directing agent.  Field emission SEM (FESEM), transmission electron microscopy (TEM) and high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM) analyses showed that SnO microspheres consist of nanosheets with a thickness of about 20 nm.  Each nanosheet contains a mesoporous structure with a pore size of approx. 5 nm.  When applied as anode materials in Na-ion batteries, SnO microspheres exhibited high reversible sodium storage capacity, good cyclability and a satisfactory high rate performance.  Through ex situ XRD anal., it was found that Na+ ions first insert themselves into SnO crystals, and then react with SnO to generate cryst. Sn, followed by Na-Sn alloying with the formation of cryst. NaSn2 phase.  During the charge process, there are two slopes corresponding to the de-alloying of Na-Sn compds. and oxidization of Sn, resp.  The high sodium storage capacity and good electrochem. performance could be ascribed to the unique hierarchical mesoporous architecture of SnO microspheres.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrXdrhnu8DXbLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljpEJxaYHLOGg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXisFWiu78%253D&amp;md5=744dcb004cf9eba80fc40d876769c221</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref55" class="rightTabRefNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit55" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201401123"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">3D Porous γ-Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@C Nanocomposite as High-Performance Anode Material of Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. Energy Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1401123</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        <script nonce="90f6edf73e9d775c-SJC">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

        <span class="system-message-date">Sunday, February 09, 2025</span>
        <p>Please be aware that pubs.acs.org is undergoing maintenance from Saturday February 1 to Monday Febraury 3, that may have an impact on your experience. During this time, you may not be able to access certain features like login, purchasing single articles, saving searches or running existing saved searches, modifying your e-Alert preferences, or accessing Librarian administrative functions. <script nonce="90f6edf73e9d775c-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

                    
                        



        
        <!-- Hotjar Tracking Code for https://pubs.acs.org/ -->

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6edf73e9d775c-SJC">
"use strict"
//Script checks gdpr cookie and submits form
	/* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.
	 
	Needs the end point
	*/

var infoCentralCapture = (function() {

    //Detect mobile device
    window.mobilecheck = function() {
        var check = false;
        (function(a){if(/(android|bb\d+|meego).+mobile|avantgo|bada\/|blackberry|blazer|compal|elaine|fennec|hiptop|iemobile|ip(hone|od)|iris|kindle|lge |maemo|midp|mmp|mobile.+firefox|netfront|opera wa|abac|ac(er|oo|s\-)|ai(ko|rn)|al(av|ca|co)|amoi|an(ex|ny|yw)|aptu|ar(ch|go)|as(te|us)|attw|au(di|\-m|r |s )|avan|be(ck|ll|nq)|bi(lb|rd)|bl(ac|az)|br(e|v)w|bumb|bw\-(n|u)|c55\/|capi|ccwa|cdm\-|cell|chtm|cldc|cmd\-|co(mp|nd)|craw|da(it|ll|ng)|dbte|dc\-s|devi|dica|dmob|do(c|p)o|ds(12|\-d)|el(49|ai)|em(l2|ul)|er(ic|k0)|esl8|ez([4-7]0|os|wa|ze)|fetc|fly(\-|_)|g1 u|g560|gene|gf\-5|g\-mo|go(\.w|od)|gr(ad|un)|haie|hcit|hd\-(m|p|t)|hei\-|hi(pt|ta)|hp( i|ip)|hs\-c|ht(c(\-| |_|a|g|p|s|t)|tp)|hu(aw|tc)|i\-(20|go|ma)|i230|iac( |\-|\/)|ibro|idea|ig01|ikom|im1k|inno|ipaq|iris|ja(t|v)a|jbro|jemu|jigs|kddi|keji|kgt( |\/)|klon|kpt |kwc\-|kyo(c|k)|le(no|xi)|lg( g|\/(k|l|u)|50|54|\-[a-w])|libw|lynx|m1\-w|m3ga|m50\/|ma(te|ui|xo)|mc(01|21|ca)|m\-cr|me(rc|ri)|mi(o8|oa|ts)|mmef|mo(01|02|bi|de|do|t(\-| |o|v)|zz)|mt(50|p1|v )|mwbp|mywa|n10[0-2]|n20[2-3]|n30(0|2)|n50(0|2|5)|n7(0(0|1)|10)|ne((c|m)\-|on|tf|wf|wg|wt)|nok(6|i)|nzph|o2im|op(ti|wv)|oran|owg1|p800|pan(a|d|t)|pdxg|pg(13|\-([1-8]|c))|phil|pire|pl(ay|uc)|pn\-2|po(ck|rt|se)|prox|psio|pt\-g|qa\-a|qc(07|12|21|32|60|\-[2-7]|i\-)|qtek|r380|r600|raks|rim9|ro(ve|zo)|s55\/|sa(ge|ma|mm|ms|ny|va)|sc(01|h\-|oo|p\-)|sdk\/|se(c(\-|0|1)|47|mc|nd|ri)|sgh\-|shar|sie(\-|m)|sk\-0|sl(45|id)|sm(al|ar|b3|it|t5)|so(ft|ny)|sp(01|h\-|v\-|v )|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>


                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="90f6edf73e9d775c-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Nano";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>

                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="90f6edf73e9d775c-SJC">
$(document).ready(function(){
    var cookie = "";
    var uri = "/doi/full/10.1021/html_original_uri?id=123";
    console.log("ACSPubs2 start");
    $.getJSON('https://extreme-ip-lookup.com/json/', function(data, status) {
            if ( status == 'success' ) {
                $.each(data, function(i, field){
                    cookie=cookie.concat(i+' = '+field+" - ");
                });
                
            } else {
                    cookie=status;
            }

            cookie1 = cookie;
            cookie = cookie1 + "; path=/; domain=.acs.org";
            //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
            $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
            //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
            console.log("ACSPubs2 success");
    })
    .fail(function(xx, status, err){
        cookie="error: 127.0.0.1";
        //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
        $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
        console.log("ACSPubs2 failed");
        //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
    });
});    
</script>
